  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_406a16c7-a93c-4b72-8b7c-2d2eab7d1a22'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText6449538346354219467" style="display:none">CHERUB agents are all seventeen and under. They wear skate tees and hemp, and look like regular kids. But they're not. They are trained professionals who are sent out on missions to spy on terrorists and international drug dealers. CHERUB agents hack into computers, bug entire houses, and download crucial documents. It is a highly dangerous job. For their safety, these agents DO NOT EXIST.<br /><br />Mainstream animal protection groups have always stayed within the law, but a new band of radical liberationists argues that if humans and animals are equal, then it's right to kill or threaten one human in order to save the lives of many animals. In a new mission, James and the other CHERUB agents must go up against the most radical group yet in a daring and violent attempt to save hundreds of lives . . . including their own.</span>

    <a title="Jonathan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12336422-jonathan"><img alt="Jonathan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346280683p2/12336422.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/427882557?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonathan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonathan" href="/user/show/12336422-jonathan">Jonathan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer427882557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5038433441948293863">Man vs. Beast, the sixth book in the CHERUB series, is, in my opinion, the best and most interesting book Robert Muchamore has written. This science fiction story is compared by many to the Alex Rider series. The plot of both of these stories is centered on a young character that is a British spy. In Man vs. Beast, James, the main character is sent on a mission to infiltrate a group of environmental extremists. Throughout the story, the reasons for animal rights protestors are depicted, and Jame</span>
  <span id="freeText5038433441948293863" style="display:none">Man vs. Beast, the sixth book in the CHERUB series, is, in my opinion, the best and most interesting book Robert Muchamore has written. This science fiction story is compared by many to the Alex Rider series. The plot of both of these stories is centered on a young character that is a British spy. In Man vs. Beast, James, the main character is sent on a mission to infiltrate a group of environmental extremists. Throughout the story, the reasons for animal rights protestors are depicted, and James’ sister, Lauren, is convinced to turn vegan. As James delves deeper into the secret society of extremists, the stakes get higher. One of my favorite aspects of this story is how suspenseful it is. Imagine this: three British secret agents, inside a top- secret organization in the process of carrying out a highly illegal crime, just waiting to suddenly turn hostile and overpower the villains. In the end, this book is just awesome. With so many plot twists, suspenseful moments, and unexpected events, this book is definitely worth reading, especially if you like James Bond. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5038433441948293863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13189481182603624389">This book is the sixth book in the CHERUB series by Robert Muchamore. In this series what I enjoy is that children and teenagers are the spies and not just adults, but both the children and adults are working side by side together to get the bad guys.   <span id="freeText13189481182603624389" style="display:none">This book is the sixth book in the CHERUB series by Robert Muchamore. In this series what I enjoy is that children and teenagers are the spies and not just adults, but both the children and adults are working side by side together to get the bad guys. Not only do I think this is interesting, but also unlike some other books about kid spies, the children and teens in this book still act like their age. The children don’t act like grown adults yet and are still experiencing an every day teen problems, with the crazy missions on the side to all this. This book is all about how the children spies get sent out to uncover an organization that kills people to protect animals from people. They uncover and organization called PETA, they are all about animal freedom, and they go around killing people who test bad things on animals that can kill them. This was a really good book that I think if people read and liked the Alex Rider series by Anthony Horowitz they should definitely read this series.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4450706925602726384">I LOVE THIS SERIES! And this book was yet another great addition to the series. Fast paced and exciting, each book on this series is completely different from the one before it with just the great characters and the a great premise of child spies to hold it all together. As much as I would love to read the next book in the series NOW I'm going to wait as long as possible because I know this series is going to end. <br/><br/>The main characters remain to be the Adams siblings, James and Lauren, now both Ch</span>
  <span id="freeText4450706925602726384" style="display:none">I LOVE THIS SERIES! And this book was yet another great addition to the series. Fast paced and exciting, each book on this series is completely different from the one before it with just the great characters and the a great premise of child spies to hold it all together. As much as I would love to read the next book in the series NOW I'm going to wait as long as possible because I know this series is going to end. <br /><br />The main characters remain to be the Adams siblings, James and Lauren, now both Cherub agents and at the start of the book causing havoc on the campus. They go off on mission, this time to an animal rights activist group which they have to infiltrate. James and Lauren are both growing up, this was evident in this book with Lauren gaining a romantic interest and James maturing hugely. <br /><br />There are a lot of secondary characters in this book but the main ones for me are the other members of team Cherub and I have already reviewed them or probably will in the other books in the series. <br /><br />The storyline with this book is as original as all the others before it; but this is the first book in the series where I have actually noticed real character development with the main characters. The pacing is excellent and I look forward to reading more books in the series. <br /><br />4 stars</span>

    <a title="Clare Carter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24985536-clare-carter"><img alt="Clare Carter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515628286p2/24985536.jpg" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer13057982667539006661">*3.5 stars*<br/><br/>I feel like my reviews for these books are getting a tad repetitive, so I'll try to change it up a little here. I have noticed something over the course of the books, and especially in this one: James is an ass (like I've mentioned), but the author knows he's an ass. Like, all the other characters are constantly telling him to get over his ego. Even though I wish he'd go through a TOUCH more character development, I do appreciate him as a complex character. <br/><br/>Anyway, as for this book sp</span>
  <span id="freeText13057982667539006661" style="display:none">*3.5 stars*<br /><br />I feel like my reviews for these books are getting a tad repetitive, so I'll try to change it up a little here. I have noticed something over the course of the books, and especially in this one: James is an ass (like I've mentioned), but the author knows he's an ass. Like, all the other characters are constantly telling him to get over his ego. Even though I wish he'd go through a TOUCH more character development, I do appreciate him as a complex character. <br /><br />Anyway, as for this book specifically, I enjoyed it, but it was a bit more gruesome than some of the others and I didn't enjoy the plot as much as the last one or the prison one (Maximum Security, I think that one's called?) I'm still in it to win it for this series. Maybe I'll have them all done by the end of the summer... </span>
  <a data-text-id="13057982667539006661" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8989982912432410658" style="display:none">The book Man VS Beast by Robert Muchamore is a very good book for action and for undercover kid agents out working for the British government. In Man VS Beast, the three kid agents went on a mission with an vegetarian man who is part of a alliance that is trying to earn rights for experiment animals in labs. The main character is James. For James he loved to eat meat and was hard since James mostly ate meat for food and was difficult for James to adjust to the vegetarian food because the man they had the mission with was a vegetarian and only hand vegetarian food. By the time the mission was done his little sister Lauren went from eating meat and dead animal to being a vegetarian and trying to spread it to her friends. The final agent was Kyle who was James’s gay friend. As for Kyle in his last moments of the mission, he had to go against something he wished he never did. But overall the book was great. I would give is a 8.5 out of 10 and would recommend it to people who love action and thrilling moments.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1025903179" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1025903179" />
    <a title="Catherine Muldoon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17041753-catherine-muldoon"><img alt="Catherine Muldoon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1359750206p2/17041753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1025903179?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catherine Muldoon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catherine Muldoon" href="/user/show/17041753-catherine-muldoon">Catherine Muldoon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1025903179" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5240513674168693593">It seems like any normal weekday, kids getting ready for school, parent organising themselves for another work shift. How could anything go wrong? A slow day flips into a dash of violent attacks on Andy and Stuart Pierce's mum with red paint supposing to symbolise blood. As a matter of fact, Christine Pierce works at Malarek Research centre which is a laboratory for testing on animals, so not everyone will be pleased on that. Especially animal activist groups or animal extremists. This fast pace</span>
  <span id="freeText5240513674168693593" style="display:none">It seems like any normal weekday, kids getting ready for school, parent organising themselves for another work shift. How could anything go wrong? A slow day flips into a dash of violent attacks on Andy and Stuart Pierce's mum with red paint supposing to symbolise blood. As a matter of fact, Christine Pierce works at Malarek Research centre which is a laboratory for testing on animals, so not everyone will be pleased on that. Especially animal activist groups or animal extremists. This fast paced section at the end of chapter 1 questions yourself, who the guys in the balaclavas were? etc., but altogether it makes you read on. <br /><br />James Adams is 14, at this point he is on his 6th mission with Cherub. The mission to unearth the Animal Freedom Milta. As pointed, <i>adults never suspect that children are spying on them</i>. Yet this comes with difficult challenges fitting in. The task is set for James Adams, his sister Lauren and his (gay) friend Kyle. All face troubles and their demons of meat slaughter (James and Lauren), boyfriends(Kyle), animal cruelty (Lauren) and chances of human murder within the task (James and Kyle). At first I thought Robert Muchamore, was focusing on the character Lauren due to the little mission at the beginning, her punishment and her window smashed in, which is an interesting take. Nonetheless it refocuses on James and Kyle and Lauren doesn't have a major role, despite her being a black shirt. <br /><br />Altogether the last 25% I could not stop reading or slow down as excitement levels rose. However, it doesn't mean the last 25%, the other 75% wasn't good, it was fantastic and well written. Overall, my favourite scene was the minor mission to help the new recruits and the extremist's group actions on the last few chapters.<br /><br />The book includes all the action, excitement and tense situations of the CHERUB series so far, moreover it adds bits of information on vegetarianism and animal cruelty. In addition to the thrill that any teenager loves to read, Man Vs Beast will truly make you think about your beliefs of animal testing and cruelty. On the other hand, as much as I liked this book, I have a feeling Divine Madness (clue in the name) has the most excitable ending in the Cherub series. <br /><br />To not end on a bad note. All of the elements of a good cherub book are definitely included in the book, it makes this novel worthwhile to read. Overall the whole mysterious story was well written for a mixed variety of genres. This' book target audience is for teens mainly boys, but I believe this can be enjoyed by female teenagers as well. I enjoyed every single novel of the cherub series so far and would definitely recommended the whole series.<br /><br /><b>This is a book you can lost in and let hours pass and is the series that started me to read again. TRUALLY RECOMMEND.</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5240513674168693593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1363735845" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1363735845" />
    <a title="Cal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45939145-cal"><img alt="Cal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439568493p2/45939145.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1363735845?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cal" href="/user/show/45939145-cal">Cal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1363735845" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10720591846559552417">Man vs Beast by Robert Muchamore is the story of James, Kyle, and Lauren, as they try to infiltrate and destroy a secret organization of terrorist who try to end animal suffering anyway possible. <br/>One of the main characters, Lauren, is a young girl who is subjected to many influences in her lifetime. She is told on missions to not believe most of the things she hears while with some of the crazies. But with some animal right activists she is persuaded into seeing eye to eye with animal activists.</span>
  <span id="freeText10720591846559552417" style="display:none">Man vs Beast by Robert Muchamore is the story of James, Kyle, and Lauren, as they try to infiltrate and destroy a secret organization of terrorist who try to end animal suffering anyway possible. <br />One of the main characters, Lauren, is a young girl who is subjected to many influences in her lifetime. She is told on missions to not believe most of the things she hears while with some of the crazies. But with some animal right activists she is persuaded into seeing eye to eye with animal activists. She agreed with the crazies she was meant to get information on to put them in jail but she thought they also had some points she agreed with. Even though most of them were insane she was able to see past the bad parts and look at the good stuff. A big part when heading into adulthood being able to look past the worst in someone to find the one good that you can pay attention to.<br />In my life I've never been able to look past the worst in someone I always focus on the worst in people and a skill i need to work on is being able to see the best in everyone. I think I do this because I have a lot of problems with trusting people. In order to become a better adult I must be able to put my trust into the people who have good in them, but I first must learn to find the good inside the person to fully trust them.<br />I would recommend this book to all people who enjoy adventure and are interested in animal rights because that topic is heavily covered in this book. This book has easy to understand language but at times can be confusing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10720591846559552417" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer813454932" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9407063152672769482"> The book I read was Man VS. Beast by Robert Muchamore. This book did not have a central idea or message. This book takes place in many places that are not stated, in a year that is not specified but in the early two thousands. This book is written in the limited sense of a boy named James and his sister named Lauren. James and Lauren are both blond haired children, James is a fourteen year old, while Lauren is a twelve year old. In this book James, Lauren and some other characters go on a missi</span>
  <span id="freeText9407063152672769482" style="display:none"> The book I read was Man VS. Beast by Robert Muchamore. This book did not have a central idea or message. This book takes place in many places that are not stated, in a year that is not specified but in the early two thousands. This book is written in the limited sense of a boy named James and his sister named Lauren. James and Lauren are both blond haired children, James is a fourteen year old, while Lauren is a twelve year old. In this book James, Lauren and some other characters go on a mission to discover the leader of a terrorist group.<br /><br /> I really liked this book because of the way it was written and because I can kind of relate to one of the characters. One of my favorite parts of the book is when James takes down to adults by himself, "He snatched Adelaide's wrist and twisted her arm up behind her back and clamped the wet cloth over her mouth with the other…. but Mark was scrawny and James to wriggle out of the clumsy hold and land a better punch with his empty hand." This is my favorite part because it shows that size does not always matter in a fight. I do not come to realize anything after reading this book because it is not the type of book that teaches you something. I think some of the strengths of this book are the way it is written, the characters, and the genre. I do not think this book has any weaknesses. I would recommend this book to anyone who likes action and a little adventure.<br /><br /> </span>

          </span>

    <a title="Andrew G" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59013982-andrew-g"><img alt="Andrew G" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1770695424?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew G" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew G" href="/user/show/59013982-andrew-g">Andrew G</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1770695424" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18192867150286812859">Man vs. Beast by Robert Muchamore was a great action and adventure book. The author wanted to let people know that it's ok to do the right thing, but violence is not the solution. Most of the story takes places in a little town in England, and a house in that town that is being rented out by Cherub agents James, Lauren and Kyle, along with Ryan Quinn, an insider, and Zara Asker, a mission helper. James, Lauren and Kyle are on a mission to befriend members of the AFA, and eventually become a memb</span>
  <span id="freeText18192867150286812859" style="display:none">Man vs. Beast by Robert Muchamore was a great action and adventure book. The author wanted to let people know that it's ok to do the right thing, but violence is not the solution. Most of the story takes places in a little town in England, and a house in that town that is being rented out by Cherub agents James, Lauren and Kyle, along with Ryan Quinn, an insider, and Zara Asker, a mission helper. James, Lauren and Kyle are on a mission to befriend members of the AFA, and eventually become a member of the AFA, which is a group that violently destroys companies that are mistreating animals for testing and other things. Once they are in, they have to overthrow the group, by going on one of there violent acts on a celebrity who owns one of those companies. This book always kept me wanting to read more, and made you more nervous about what was going to happen every page. The overall plot was sort of boring, especially compared to the other books in this series, but it was overall a great book, and I would recommend it to anyone who loves fast paced action/adventure books.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_287533378" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/287533378" />
    <a title="Kathy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4237625-kathy"><img alt="Kathy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286028287p2/4237625.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/287533378?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy" href="/user/show/4237625-kathy">Kathy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781416927259" href="/book/show/592805.Man_vs_Beast">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4237625-kathy?shelf=read-in-february-2012">read-in-february-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer287533378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3603668277699036989">You know, I'd like to give some of these a two, but they are good reads. Not great literature, not all time classics, but good solid reads. The characters are pretty well developed (especially if you've been following the whole series), and the plots, once you swallow the main premise, unfold realistically. James, our 14 year old main hero is no saint, nor does he have any super-normal skills, and he does have his share of prejudices and bad habits. But he remains likeable.<br/><br/>Anyway, this time out </span>
  <span id="freeText3603668277699036989" style="display:none">You know, I'd like to give some of these a two, but they are good reads. Not great literature, not all time classics, but good solid reads. The characters are pretty well developed (especially if you've been following the whole series), and the plots, once you swallow the main premise, unfold realistically. James, our 14 year old main hero is no saint, nor does he have any super-normal skills, and he does have his share of prejudices and bad habits. But he remains likeable.<br /><br />Anyway, this time out CHERUB is pitted against animal rights terrorists. You know the drill.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3151594694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2339776499592246973">Whilst the book was entertaining, the CHERUB formula is getting a bit stale for me at this point... I definitely felt the whole animal cruelty and abuse aspect could have been explored a lot deeper, despite a few standout moments. The last third really ramped up the excitement, but the rest felt a bit underdeveloped, especially in the character interactions. It doesn't help that James really isn't changing as a character, and seems to get away fine with this behaviour. The rest was fun, includin</span>
  <span id="freeText2339776499592246973" style="display:none">Whilst the book was entertaining, the CHERUB formula is getting a bit stale for me at this point... I definitely felt the whole animal cruelty and abuse aspect could have been explored a lot deeper, despite a few standout moments. The last third really ramped up the excitement, but the rest felt a bit underdeveloped, especially in the character interactions. It doesn't help that James really isn't changing as a character, and seems to get away fine with this behaviour. The rest was fun, including the village setting and handful of action scenes - just pretty forgettable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2339776499592246973" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7825734176172853402">I like this book as I think that it was quite interesting. Cherub agents go on a mission to become undercover agents as children. This book is in the crime genre and is about how the animal freedom people try to get animals from the animal scientists. This is the sixth book of the Cherub Series. This is a crime story which is exciting but can be hard to follow. I would recommend to teenagers as there is some bad language.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Z6HJpRXqPKY7Mw5O9f3mp9S3+XYTgJ3X3cLb7/5fVD7s06HX3z6k18Qs1qkY2ElC538ya5HhRx8hOkxtV07sCg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cYtXArzR4XWRjwNhbCl7ezqd03VHlekPrTOvTZw22vr6+T9wdgV5BG6Q24aBDNSeCVUYaMX0M8dRyzjPNSdizg==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2535621329868642726">Robert Muchamore was born in Islington, London in 1972. He still lives there, and worked as a private investigator up until 2005 and the critically-accepted release of <i>Maximum Security</i>. <br/><br/>The Hunger Games phenomenon is part of the huge YA / Children's book explosion that has grown, thanks to the British Rat pack of YA authors, Anthony Horowitz, Robert Muchamore, Mark A. Cooper and Charlie Higson. We</span>
  <span id="freeText2535621329868642726" style="display:none">Robert Muchamore was born in Islington, London in 1972. He still lives there, and worked as a private investigator up until 2005 and the critically-accepted release of <i>Maximum Security</i>. <br /><br />The Hunger Games phenomenon is part of the huge YA / Children's book explosion that has grown, thanks to the British Rat pack of YA authors, Anthony Horowitz, Robert Muchamore, Mark A. Cooper and Charlie Higson. We owe much of the hunger games sucess to authors such as Robert.<br /><br />Robert was inspired to create the CHERUB series by his nephew after he complained about the lack of anything for them to read. CHERUB: The Recruit was Robert's first book and won the Red House Children's Book Award 2005 in the Older Readers Category. <br /><br />Following the last book in the CHERUB series, it was revealed that a trilogy would be released starting from August 2011 that will focus on a new set of CHERUB agents centred upon Ryan Sharma and also involve an sixteen year old Lauren Adams. The first book will be called People's Republic. <br /><br />Check out the Hendersons Boys series. Henderson's Boys is a series of young adult spy novels written by English author Robert Muchamore. The series follows Charles Henderson, the creator of the fictitious CHERUB organisation. <br />CHERUB is currently being made into a TV series.</span>
